## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration-time ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of concentration A, indicating an ordinary differential equation typical of chemical kinetics. With only t and A available, the most common structures are empirical/mechanistic rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, saturation, inhibition) and sometimes explicitly on t (driving/forcing, deactivation, time-varying conditions).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate regime, e.g., surface-limited or constant feed)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order consumption)
- First-order with source term: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (net production + linear loss, chemostat-like lumping)
- Second-order loss: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or pseudo-second-order in A)
- General n-th order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting)
- Reversible approach to equilibrium (linear driving force): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-type in concentration space): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating until limited by depletion/carrying capacity)
- Saturation in A (capacity-limited rate): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates at high A due to limiting step)
- Substrate inhibition / self-inhibition: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (rate decreases at high A due to inhibitory complex formation)
- Mixed first + second order: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel pathways or combined mechanisms)
- Time-dependent deactivation of rate: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant decays in time, e.g., catalyst deactivation or fading illumination)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., modulated light/feed): dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + sin(c2 * t)) * A (externally driven time-varying first-order kinetics)
- Stretched-exponential-type kinetics (empirical time variation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t**c2) * A (distributed-rate/heterogeneous environment surrogate)
- Finite-time quench or switch-on (smooth step): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (c1 + tanh(c2 * (t - c3))) (reaction turns on/off around a characteristic time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Sign convention: consumption of A typically implies dA_dt < 0 with positive A; production implies dA_dt > 0ŌĆömodels often embed this as an explicit leading minus sign.
- Reaction order identification: linear dependence on A suggests first-order; quadratic dependence suggests second-order; fractional powers A**c capture complex/transport-limited effective orders.
- Equilibrium relaxation: dependence on (A - c) indicates approach toward a steady-state/equilibrium concentration; c is the long-time limit when no explicit t forcing remains.
- Parallel-pathway kinetics: sums of terms (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2) often indicate multiple simultaneous mechanisms contributing additively to the net rate.
- Autocatalysis signature: presence of A multiplied by (c - A) (or similar) indicates self-acceleration at low A and self-limitation at high A.
- Saturation/limitation by intermediates: rational forms with A in numerator and (A + c) or (c + A + c*A**2) in denominator indicate a fast-binding/slow-step bottleneck or inhibitory complex formation.
- Time-varying environment: explicit exp(-c*t), sin(c*t), or tanh(c*(t-c)) factors multiplying an A-dependent rate term indicate changing external conditions (light intensity, catalyst activity, feed switching).
- Early-time vs late-time regimes: models that multiply A-dependent terms by exp(-c*t) or exp(-c*t**p) encode a strong early rate that diminishes over time, matching deactivation/aging phenomena.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK29)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_z*A**c4/(c5*A**c6 + c7)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze whether any candidate can exactly match the Ground Truth (GT):

$$GT = -0.10133 \cdot A - 0.10133 \cdot A \cdot e^{-0.07564 \cdot t} + \frac{0.82602 \cdot A^2}{0.86358 \cdot A^4 + 1}$$

The GT has three components:
1. A linear term in A: $-0.10133 \cdot A$
2. An exponential-decay term: $-0.10133 \cdot A \cdot e^{-0.07564t}$
3. A rational function: $\frac{0.82602 \cdot A^2}{0.86358 \cdot A^4 + 1}$

The key challenge is matching the rational function $\frac{A^2}{c \cdot A^4 + 1}$. This is NOT a polynomial, exponential, logarithmic, trigonometric, or power-law function. Let me check which candidates could potentially represent this.

**Key observation:** The rational function $\frac{A^2}{A^4 + c}$ cannot be exactly represented by:
- Polynomials or power laws (including negative powers like $1/A$, $1/A^5$)
- Exponentials $e^{cA}$
- Logarithms $\log(cA + 1)$
- Trigonometric functions $\sin(cA + c)$
- Combinations of the above

The function $\frac{A^2}{A^4+1}$ has specific behavior: it goes to 0 as $A \to 0$, peaks, then decays as $A^{-2}$ for large $A$. No finite sum of the basis functions available in the candidates can reproduce this exactly.

Let me verify: Could sums of exponentials like $c_1 e^{c_2 A} + c_3 e^{c_4 A}$ match $\frac{A^2}{A^4+1}$? No - exponentials grow/decay monotonically and cannot match a rational function that peaks and decays algebraically.

Could $\log(cA+1)$ terms help? No - logarithms grow unboundedly while the rational function decays.

Could $1/A + 1/A^5$ terms help? These are singular at $A=0$ while the GT is smooth at $A=0$.

Could power terms like $A^{c}$ help? A single power law cannot match the non-monotonic behavior.

None of the candidates contain a rational function structure like $A^n/(A^m + c)$ or $1/(A^m + c)$ that could reproduce the GT's rational component.

Let me quickly scan all candidates to confirm none have rational function terms in A:

Going through all 50 candidates: They use combinations of $A^{1/5}$, $A^{1/3}$, $A$, $A^2$, $A^c$, $e^{cA}$, $\log(cA+1)$, $\sin(cA+c)$, $1/A$, $1/A^5$, $1/(A+c)$, $e^{ct}$, $1/(c+t)^3$, and polynomial terms. 

Candidate 22 has $1/(A+c_7)$ - but this is $\frac{1}{A+c}$, not $\frac{A^2}{A^4+c}$. These are fundamentally different rational functions.

None of the candidates contain the necessary $\frac{A^2}{A^4 + c}$ structure or any combination of terms that could algebraically simplify to it.
